	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" >Vint Cerf</h1>
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>

		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">American computer scientist</div>

<p><b>Vinton Gray Cerf</b><sup id="cite_ref-vita_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vita-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> <span class="noexcerpt nowraplinks" style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Foreign_Member_of_the_Royal_Society" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign Member of the Royal Society">ForMemRS</a></span><sup id="cite_ref-frs_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frs-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/ɜːr/: &#39;ur&#39; in &#39;fur&#39;">ɜːr</span><span title="&#39;f&#39; in &#39;find&#39;">f</span></span>/</a></span></span>; born June 23, 1943) is an American <a href="/wiki/Internet_pioneer" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet pioneer">Internet pioneer</a> and is recognized as one of "<a href="/wiki/List_of_Internet_pioneers" title="List of Internet pioneers">the fathers of the Internet</a>", sharing this title with <a href="/wiki/TCP/IP" class="mw-redirect" title="TCP/IP">TCP/IP</a> co-developer <a href="/wiki/Bob_Kahn" title="Bob Kahn">Bob Kahn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He has received honorary degrees and awards that include the <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="National Medal of Technology">National Medal of Technology</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-vita_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vita-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Turing_Award" title="Turing Award">Turing Award</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-turing_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turing-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom" title="Presidential Medal of Freedom">Presidential Medal of Freedom</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-whitehouse_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whitehouse-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Marconi_Prize" title="Marconi Prize">Marconi Prize</a> and membership in the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Engineering" title="National Academy of Engineering">National Academy of Engineering</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_and_career">Life and career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vint_Cerf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Life and career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vint_Cerf_-_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Vint_Cerf_-_2010.jpg/220px-Vint_Cerf_-_2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Vint_Cerf_-_2010.jpg/330px-Vint_Cerf_-_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Vint_Cerf_-_2010.jpg/440px-Vint_Cerf_-_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2790" data-file-height="2791" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vint_Cerf_-_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vinton Cerf in <a href="/wiki/Vilnius" title="Vilnius">Vilnius</a>, September 2010</div></div></div>
<p>Cerf was born in <a href="/wiki/New_Haven,_Connecticut" title="New Haven, Connecticut">New Haven, Connecticut</a>, the son of Muriel (née Gray) and Vinton Thurston Cerf.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Cerf attended <a href="/wiki/Van_Nuys_High_School" title="Van Nuys High School">Van Nuys High School</a> with <a href="/wiki/Jon_Postel" title="Jon Postel">Jon Postel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Crocker" title="Steve Crocker">Steve Crocker</a>. While in high school, Cerf worked at <a href="/wiki/Rocketdyne" title="Rocketdyne">Rocketdyne</a> on the Apollo program and helped write statistical analysis software for the non-destructive tests of the <a href="/wiki/Rocketdyne_F-1" title="Rocketdyne F-1">F-1 engines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cerf received a Bachelor of Science degree in mathematics from <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> After college, Cerf worked at <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Systems_engineer" class="mw-redirect" title="Systems engineer">systems engineer</a> supporting <a href="/wiki/QUIKTRAN" title="QUIKTRAN">QUIKTRAN</a> for two years.<sup id="cite_ref-vita_2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vita-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cerf  and his wife Sigrid both have hearing deficiencies; they met at a <a href="/wiki/Hearing_aid" title="Hearing aid">hearing aid</a> agent's practice in the 1960s,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> which led him to becoming an advocate for accessibility.
</p><p>He left IBM to attend graduate school at <a href="/wiki/UCLA" class="mw-redirect" title="UCLA">UCLA</a> where he earned his M.S. degree in 1970 and his PhD in 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-cerfphd_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cerfphd-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UCLAEngineering2005_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCLAEngineering2005-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Cerf studied under Professor <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Estrin" title="Gerald Estrin">Gerald Estrin</a> and worked in Professor <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Kleinrock" title="Leonard Kleinrock">Leonard Kleinrock</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Data_packet" class="mw-redirect" title="Data packet">data packet</a> networking group that connected the first two nodes of the <a href="/wiki/ARPANet" class="mw-redirect" title="ARPANet">ARPANet</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-CNN1999_09_02_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN1999_09_02-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> the first node<sup id="cite_ref-CNN1999_09_02_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN1999_09_02-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> on the Internet, and "contributed to a host-to-host protocol" for the ARPANet.<sup id="cite_ref-ACM2005_02_16_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACM2005_02_16-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While at <a href="/wiki/UCLA" class="mw-redirect" title="UCLA">UCLA</a>, Cerf met <a href="/wiki/Bob_Kahn" title="Bob Kahn">Bob Kahn</a>, who was working on the <a href="/wiki/ARPANet" class="mw-redirect" title="ARPANet">ARPANet</a> system architecture.<sup id="cite_ref-ACM2005_02_16_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACM2005_02_16-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Cerf wrote the first <a href="/wiki/TCP/IP" class="mw-redirect" title="TCP/IP">TCP</a> protocol with Yogen Dalal and Carl Sunshine, called <i>Specification of Internet Transmission Control Program</i> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r999302996">.mw-parser-output cite.citation{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .citation q{quotes:"\"""\"""'""'"}.mw-parser-output .id-lock-free a,.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-free a{background:linear-gradient(transparent,transparent),url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/65/Lock-green.svg")right 0.1em center/9px no-repeat}.mw-parser-output .id-lock-limited a,.mw-parser-output .id-lock-registration a,.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-limited a,.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-registration a{background:linear-gradient(transparent,transparent),url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d6/Lock-gray-alt-2.svg")right 0.1em center/9px no-repeat}.mw-parser-output .id-lock-subscription a,.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-subscription a{background:linear-gradient(transparent,transparent),url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/aa/Lock-red-alt-2.svg")right 0.1em center/9px no-repeat}.mw-parser-output .cs1-subscription,.mw-parser-output .cs1-registration{color:#555}.mw-parser-output .cs1-subscription span,.mw-parser-output .cs1-registration span{border-bottom:1px dotted;cursor:help}.mw-parser-output .cs1-ws-icon a{background:linear-gradient(transparent,transparent),url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg")right 0.1em center/12px no-repeat}.mw-parser-output code.cs1-code{color:inherit;background:inherit;border:none;padding:inherit}.mw-parser-output .cs1-hidden-error{display:none;font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .cs1-visible-error{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .cs1-maint{display:none;color:#33aa33;margin-left:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .cs1-format{font-size:95%}.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-left,.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-wl-left{padding-left:0.2em}.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-right,.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-wl-right{padding-right:0.2em}.mw-parser-output .citation .mw-selflink{font-weight:inherit}</style><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc675">675</a>), published in December 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cerf worked as <a href="/wiki/Professor#Assistant_professor" title="Professor">assistant professor</a> at Stanford University from 1972 to 1976 where he conducted research on packet network interconnection protocols and co-designed the DoD TCP/IP protocol suite with Kahn.<sup id="cite_ref-ACM2005_02_16_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACM2005_02_16-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vinton_Cerf-20070512.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Vinton_Cerf-20070512.jpg/220px-Vinton_Cerf-20070512.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="327" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Vinton_Cerf-20070512.jpg/330px-Vinton_Cerf-20070512.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Vinton_Cerf-20070512.jpg/440px-Vinton_Cerf-20070512.jpg 2x" data-file-width="689" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vinton_Cerf-20070512.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cerf playing <i><a href="/wiki/Spacewar_(video_game)" class="mw-redirect" title="Spacewar (video game)">Spacewar!</a></i> on the <a href="/wiki/Computer_History_Museum" title="Computer History Museum">Computer History Museum</a>'s <a href="/wiki/PDP-1" title="PDP-1">PDP-1</a>, <a href="/wiki/ICANN" title="ICANN">ICANN</a> meeting, 2007</div></div></div>
<p>Cerf worked at the United States <a href="/wiki/DARPA" title="DARPA">Defense Advanced Research Projects Agency</a> (DARPA) from 1973 to 1982 and funded various groups to develop <a href="/wiki/TCP/IP" class="mw-redirect" title="TCP/IP">TCP/IP</a>, packet radio (<a href="/wiki/PRNET" title="PRNET">PRNET</a>), packet satellite (<a href="/wiki/SATNET" title="SATNET">SATNET</a>) and packet security technology.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> These efforts were rooted in the needs of the military.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In the late 1980s, Cerf moved to <a href="/wiki/MCI_Communications" title="MCI Communications">MCI</a> where he helped develop the first commercial email system (<a href="/wiki/MCI_Mail" title="MCI Mail">MCI Mail</a>) to be connected to the Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cerf is active in a number of global humanitarian organizations.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Cerf is also known for his <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/sartorial" class="extiw" title="wikt:sartorial">sartorial</a> style, typically appearing in a <a href="/wiki/Three-piece_suit" class="mw-redirect" title="Three-piece suit">three-piece suit</a>—a rarity in an industry known for its casual dress norms.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As vice president of MCI Digital Information Services from 1982 to 1986, Cerf led the engineering of <a href="/wiki/MCI_Mail" title="MCI Mail">MCI Mail</a>, the first commercial email service to be connected to the Internet. In 1986, he joined Bob Kahn at the Corporation for National Research Initiatives as its vice president, working with Kahn on Digital Libraries, Knowledge Robots, and gigabit speed networks. Since 1988 Cerf lobbied for the privatization of the internet.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In 1992, he and Kahn, among others, founded the <a href="/wiki/Internet_Society" title="Internet Society">Internet Society</a> (ISOC) to provide leadership in education, policy and standards related to the Internet. Cerf served as the first president of ISOC. Cerf rejoined MCI during 1994 and served as Senior Vice President of Technology Strategy. In this role, he helped to guide corporate strategy development from a technical perspective. Previously, he served as MCI's senior vice president of Architecture and Technology, leading a team of architects and engineers to design advanced networking frameworks, including Internet-based solutions for delivering a combination of data, information, voice and video services for business and consumer use.
</p><p>During 1997, Cerf joined the Board of Trustees of <a href="/wiki/Gallaudet_University" title="Gallaudet University">Gallaudet University</a>, a university for the education of the deaf and hard-of-hearing.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Cerf himself is hard of hearing.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>  He has also served on the university's Board of Associates.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cerf, as leader of MCI's internet business, was criticized due to MCI's role in providing the IP addresses used by Send-Safe.com, a vendor of spamware that uses a <a href="/wiki/Botnet" title="Botnet">botnet</a> in order to send spam. MCI refused to terminate the spamware vendor.<sup id="cite_ref-spamcomplaintdraft_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spamcomplaintdraft-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> At the time, <a href="/wiki/The_Spamhaus_Project" title="The Spamhaus Project">Spamhaus</a> also listed MCI as the ISP with the most Spamhaus Block List listings.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cerf has worked for <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> as a vice president and Chief <a href="/wiki/Technology_evangelist" title="Technology evangelist">Internet Evangelist</a> since October 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-google_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-google-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In this function he has become well known for his predictions on how technology will affect future society, encompassing such areas as <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>, environmentalism, the advent of <a href="/wiki/IPv6" title="IPv6">IPv6</a> and the transformation of the television industry and its delivery model.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2010, Cerf has served as a Commissioner for the <a href="/wiki/Broadband_Commission_for_Digital_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Broadband Commission for Digital Development">Broadband Commission for Digital Development</a>, a UN body which aims to make broadband internet technologies more widely available.
</p><p>Cerf helped fund and establish <a href="/wiki/ICANN" title="ICANN">ICANN</a>, the Internet Corporation for Assigned Names and Numbers.  He joined the board in 1999, and served until November 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> He was chairman from November 2000 to his departure from the Board.
</p><p>Cerf was a member of Bulgarian President <a href="/wiki/Georgi_Parvanov" title="Georgi Parvanov">Georgi Parvanov</a>'s IT Advisory Council (from March 2002 – January 2012). He is also a member of the Advisory Board of <a href="/wiki/Eurasia_Group" title="Eurasia Group">Eurasia Group</a>, the political risk consultancy.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cerf is also working on the <a href="/wiki/Interplanetary_Internet" title="Interplanetary Internet">Interplanetary Internet</a>, together with <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">Jet Propulsion Laboratory</a> and other NASA laboratories. It will be a new standard to communicate from planet to planet, using radio/laser communications that are tolerant of signal degradations including variable delay and disruption caused, for example, by celestial motion.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 7, 2006, Cerf testified before the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Senate_Committee_on_Commerce" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Senate Committee on Commerce">U.S. Senate Committee on Commerce, Science, and Transportation</a>'s hearing on <a href="/wiki/Network_neutrality" class="mw-redirect" title="Network neutrality">network neutrality</a>. Speaking as Google's Chief Internet Evangelist, Cerf noted that nearly half of all consumers lacked meaningful choice in broadband providers and expressed concerns that without network neutrality government regulation, broadband providers would be able to use their dominance to limit options for consumers and charge companies like Google for their use of bandwidth.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:VintCerfJI3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/VintCerfJI3.jpg/220px-VintCerfJI3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/VintCerfJI3.jpg/330px-VintCerfJI3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/VintCerfJI3.jpg/440px-VintCerfJI3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2252" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:VintCerfJI3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cerf at 2007 Los Angeles ICANN meeting</div></div></div>
<p>Cerf currently serves on the board of advisors of <a href="/wiki/Scientists_and_Engineers_for_America" title="Scientists and Engineers for America">Scientists and Engineers for America</a>, an organization focused on promoting sound science in American government.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> He also serves on the advisory council of <a href="/wiki/CRDF_Global" title="CRDF Global">CRDF Global</a> (Civilian Research and Development Foundation) and was on the International Multilateral Partnership Against Cyber Threats (IMPACT) International Advisory Board.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cerf was elected as the president of the <a href="/wiki/Association_for_Computing_Machinery" title="Association for Computing Machinery">Association for Computing Machinery</a> in May 2012<sup id="cite_ref-ACM_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACM-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> and joined the Council on CyberSecurity's Board of Advisors in August 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 2011 to 2016, Cerf was chairman of the board of trustees of <a href="/wiki/ARIN" class="mw-redirect" title="ARIN">ARIN</a>, the Regional Internet Registry (RIR) of IP addresses for United States, Canada, and part of the Caribbean.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Until Fall 2015, Cerf chaired the board of directors of <a href="/wiki/StopBadware" title="StopBadware">StopBadware</a>, a non-profit anti-malware organization that started as a project at Harvard University's <a href="/wiki/Berkman_Center_for_Internet_%26_Society" class="mw-redirect" title="Berkman Center for Internet &amp; Society">Berkman Center for Internet &amp; Society</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Cerf is on the board of advisors to The Liquid Information Company Ltd of the UK, which works to make the web more usefully interactive and which has produced the Mac OS X utility called 'Liquid'.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Vint Cerf is a member of the <a href="/wiki/CuriosityStream" title="CuriosityStream">CuriosityStream</a> Advisory Board.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During 2008, Cerf chaired the <a href="/wiki/Internationalized_domain_name" title="Internationalized domain name">Internationalized domain name</a> (IDNAbis) working group of the <a href="/wiki/IETF" class="mw-redirect" title="IETF">IETF</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In 2008 Cerf was a major contender to be designated the first U.S. <a href="/wiki/Chief_Technology_Officer_of_the_United_States" title="Chief Technology Officer of the United States">Chief Technology Officer</a> by President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Cerf is the co-chair of <a href="/wiki/Campus_Party" title="Campus Party">Campus Party Silicon Valley</a>, the US edition of one of the largest technology festivals in the world, along with <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tim_Berners-Lee" title="Tim Berners-Lee">Tim Berners-Lee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> From 2009 to 2011, Cerf was an elected member of the Governing Board of the <a href="/wiki/Smart_Grid_Interoperability_Panel" title="Smart Grid Interoperability Panel">Smart Grid Interoperability Panel</a> (SGIP). SGIP is a public-private consortium established by NIST in 2009 and provides a forum for businesses and other stakeholder groups to participate in coordinating and accelerating development of standards for the evolving Smart Grid.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Cerf was elected to a two-year term as President of the <a href="/wiki/Association_for_Computing_Machinery" title="Association for Computing Machinery">Association for Computing Machinery</a> (ACM) beginning July 1, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In 2015 Cerf co-founded (with Mei Lin Fung), and is currently chairman of, People-Centered Internet (PCI).<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> On January 16, 2013, U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> announced his intent to appoint Cerf to the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Board" title="National Science Board">National Science Board</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Cerf served until May 2018 when his six-year term expired.
</p><p>Cerf is also among the 15 members of governing council of <a href="/wiki/International_Institute_of_Information_Technology,_Hyderabad" title="International Institute of Information Technology, Hyderabad">International Institute of Information Technology, Hyderabad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2016, his work with NASA led to <a href="/wiki/Delay-tolerant_networking" title="Delay-tolerant networking">Delay-tolerant networking</a> being installed on the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> with an aim towards an <a href="/wiki/Interplanetary_Internet" title="Interplanetary Internet">Interplanetary Internet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NASA_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since at least 2015, Cerf has been raising concerns about the wide-ranging risks of <a href="/wiki/Digital_obsolescence" title="Digital obsolescence">digital obsolescence</a>, the potential of losing much historic information about our time – a <a href="/wiki/Digital_dark_age" title="Digital dark age">digital "dark age"</a> or "black hole" – given the ubiquitous digital storage of text, data, images, music and more. Among the concerns are the long-term storage of, and continued reliable access to, our vast stores of present-day digital data and the associated programs, operating systems, computers and peripherals required to access such.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2020, Cerf confirmed that he had tested positive for <a href="/wiki/COVID-19" class="mw-redirect" title="COVID-19">COVID-19</a>. He announced the news via a tweet in which he also criticized <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">President Donald Trump</a> for the way he was handling the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_the_United_States" title="COVID-19 pandemic in the United States">COVID-19 pandemic in the United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> On April 3, 2020, Cerf announced via Twitter that VA Public Health had certified his wife and himself as no longer contagious with the virus.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honors">Awards and honors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vint_Cerf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Awards and honors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CerfKahnMedalOfFreedom.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/CerfKahnMedalOfFreedom.jpg/220px-CerfKahnMedalOfFreedom.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/CerfKahnMedalOfFreedom.jpg/330px-CerfKahnMedalOfFreedom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/CerfKahnMedalOfFreedom.jpg/440px-CerfKahnMedalOfFreedom.jpg 2x" data-file-width="515" data-file-height="328" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CerfKahnMedalOfFreedom.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cerf and <a href="/wiki/Bob_Kahn" title="Bob Kahn">Bob E. Kahn</a> being awarded the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom" title="Presidential Medal of Freedom">Presidential Medal of Freedom</a> by President George W. Bush</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CerfParvanov.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/52/CerfParvanov.jpg/220px-CerfParvanov.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/52/CerfParvanov.jpg/330px-CerfParvanov.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/52/CerfParvanov.jpg/440px-CerfParvanov.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CerfParvanov.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cerf and Bulgarian President Parvanov being awarded the St. Cyril and Methodius in the Coat of Arms Order</div></div></div>
<p>Cerf has received a number of honorary degrees, including doctorates, from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Balearic_Islands" title="University of the Balearic Islands">University of the Balearic Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/ETHZ" class="mw-redirect" title="ETHZ">ETHZ</a> in Zurich, Switzerland, <a href="/wiki/Capitol_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Capitol College">Capitol College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gettysburg_College" title="Gettysburg College">Gettysburg College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/George_Mason_University" title="George Mason University">George Mason University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marymount_University" title="Marymount University">Marymount University</a>, Bethany College (Kansas), <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pisa" title="University of Pisa">University of Pisa</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Rovira_and_Virgili" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Rovira and Virgili">University of Rovira and Virgili</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tarragona" title="Tarragona">Tarragona</a>, Spain), <a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute" title="Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute">Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lule%C3%A5_University_of_Technology" title="Luleå University of Technology">Luleå University of Technology</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>), <a href="/wiki/University_of_Twente" title="University of Twente">University of Twente</a> (<a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>), <a href="/wiki/Beijing_University_of_Posts_and_Telecommunications" title="Beijing University of Posts and Telecommunications">Beijing University of Posts and Telecommunications</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tsinghua_University" title="Tsinghua University">Tsinghua University</a> (Beijing), <a href="/wiki/Polytechnic_University_(New_York)" class="mw-redirect" title="Polytechnic University (New York)">Brooklyn Polytechnic</a>, UPCT (University of Cartagena, Spain), Zaragoza University (Spain), <a href="/wiki/University_of_Reading" title="University of Reading">University of Reading</a> (United Kingdom), <a href="/wiki/Royal_Roads_University" title="Royal Roads University">Royal Roads University</a> (Canada), MGIMO (Moscow State University of International Relations), Buenos Aires Institute of Technology (Argentina),  <a href="/wiki/Polytechnic_University_of_Madrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Polytechnic University of Madrid">Polytechnic University of Madrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keio_University" title="Keio University">Keio University</a> (Japan), <a href="/wiki/University_of_South_Australia" title="University of South Australia">University of South Australia</a> (Australia), <a href="/wiki/University_of_St_Andrews" title="University of St Andrews">University of St Andrews</a> (Scotland), <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh">University of Pittsburgh</a> and<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gallaudet_University" title="Gallaudet University">Gallaudet University</a> (United States). Other awards include:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 35em;">
<ul><li>Edward A. Dickson Alumnus of the Year Award from UCLA<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Asturias_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince of Asturias Awards">Prince of Asturias award</a> for science and technology<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fellow_of_the_IEEE" class="mw-redirect" title="Fellow of the IEEE">Life Member IEEE</a><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Fellow of the <a href="/wiki/Association_for_Computing_Machinery" title="Association for Computing Machinery">Association for Computing Machinery</a>, 1994<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yuri_Rubinsky_Memorial_Award" title="Yuri Rubinsky Memorial Award">Yuri Rubinsky Memorial Award</a>, 1996<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SIGCOMM_Award" title="SIGCOMM Award">SIGCOMM Award</a> for "contributions to the Internet [spanning] more than 25 years, from development of the fundamental TCP/IP protocols".<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/The_Franklin_Institute_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="The Franklin Institute Awards">Certificate of Merit</a> from <a href="/wiki/The_Franklin_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="The Franklin Institute">The Franklin Institute</a>, in 1996.</li>
<li>In December 1997 he, along with his partner Robert E. Kahn, was presented with the <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="National Medal of Technology">National Medal of Technology</a> by President <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>, "for creating and sustaining development of Internet Protocols and continuing to provide leadership in the emerging industry of internetworking."<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2000, he received the honorary doctorate degree from URV, Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>He received the <a href="/wiki/Living_Legend_Medal" class="mw-redirect" title="Living Legend Medal">Living Legend Medal</a> from the Library of Congress in April 2000</li>
<li>In 2000, he was made a Fellow of the <a href="/wiki/Computer_History_Museum" title="Computer History Museum">Computer History Museum</a> "for his contributions to computer architecture, operating systems, and software engineering."<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Cerf was selected as a Fellow of the <a href="/wiki/Association_for_Women_in_Science" title="Association for Women in Science">Association for Women in Science</a> (AWIS) in 2000.</li>
<li>Cerf was awarded the Award of Technology from the Telluride Tech Festival in 2002, also known as the Tesla Festival since the world's first AC hydro-power power plant was built in Telluride in 1891 by L.L. Nunn who purchased the generator and plans from George Westinghouse and Tesla.</li>
<li>Cerf and Kahn were the winners of the <a href="/wiki/Turing_Award" title="Turing Award">Turing Award</a> for 2004,<sup id="cite_ref-turing_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turing-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> for their "pioneering work on <a href="/wiki/Internetworking" title="Internetworking">internetworking</a>, including .. the Internet's basic <a href="/wiki/Communications_protocols" class="mw-redirect" title="Communications protocols">communications protocols</a> .. and for inspired leadership in networking."<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In November 2005, Vinton Cerf and Kahn were awarded the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom" title="Presidential Medal of Freedom">Presidential Medal of Freedom</a> by President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> for their contributions to the creation of the Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-whitehouse_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whitehouse-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>He and Robert Kahn were inducted into the <a href="/wiki/National_Inventors_Hall_of_Fame" title="National Inventors Hall of Fame">National Inventors Hall of Fame</a> in May 2006</li>
<li>Vinton Cerf was awarded the St. Cyril and Methodius in the Coat of Arms Order in July 2006<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Vinton Cerf and Robert Kahn were each inducted as an Honorary Fellow of the <a href="/wiki/Society_for_Technical_Communication" title="Society for Technical Communication">Society for Technical Communication</a> (STC) in May 2006</li>
<li>He and Robert Kahn were awarded the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Prize" title="Japan Prize">Japan Prize</a> in January 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Cerf was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Worshipful_Company_of_Information_Technologists" title="Worshipful Company of Information Technologists">Worshipful Company of Information Technologists</a> and given the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_City" title="Freedom of the City">Freedom of the City</a> of London in April 2008.</li>
<li>Cerf was awarded an honorary membership in the <a href="/wiki/Yale_Political_Union" title="Yale Political Union">Yale Political Union</a> after keynoting a lively debate on the subject "Resolved: Online Communities are Real Communities." The motion passed.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In celebration of the five year-anniversary of YouTube he was selected as a guest <a href="/wiki/Curator" title="Curator">curator</a> by the site, and chose the six videos on YouTube he found most memorable.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>IEEE-HKN <a href="/wiki/Eta_Kappa_Nu" title="Eta Kappa Nu">Eta Kappa Nu</a> Eminent Member, 2010<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In May 2011, he was awarded an <a href="/wiki/Hasso_Plattner_Institute" title="Hasso Plattner Institute">HPI</a> Fellowship as "...a tribute to his work for a new medium which influenced the everyday life of our society like no other one."<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In September 2011 he was made a distinguished fellow of <a href="/wiki/British_Computer_Society" title="British Computer Society">British Computer Society</a>, in recognition of his outstanding contribution and service to the advancement of computing.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2012 he was inducted as a Pioneer into the <a href="/wiki/Internet_Hall_of_Fame" title="Internet Hall of Fame">Internet Hall of Fame</a><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2013, Cerf was one of five Internet and Web pioneers awarded the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_Prize_for_Engineering" title="Queen Elizabeth Prize for Engineering">Queen Elizabeth Prize for Engineering</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2013, Cerf presented the <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Price_Memorial_Lecture" title="Bernard Price Memorial Lecture">Bernard Price Memorial Lecture</a><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2014, Cerf was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Cross_of_Terra_Mariana" title="Order of the Cross of Terra Mariana">Order of the Cross of Terra Mariana</a>, 1st class for his role in invention of TCP/IP by president of <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a> <a href="/wiki/Toomas_Hendrik_Ilves" title="Toomas Hendrik Ilves">Toomas Hendrik Ilves</a><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2014, Cerf was awarded Officer of the <a href="/wiki/French_L%C3%A9gion_d%27honneur" class="mw-redirect" title="French Légion d&#39;honneur">French Légion d'honneur</a> <sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2015, Cerf received an honorary doctorate from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Reading" title="University of Reading">University of Reading</a>, UK.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Cerf was elected a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Fellows_of_the_Royal_Society_elected_in_2016" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Fellows of the Royal Society elected in 2016">Foreign Member of The UK Royal Society in 2016</a><sup id="cite_ref-frs_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frs-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2018, Cerf was named a recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin_Medal_(Franklin_Institute)" class="mw-redirect" title="Benjamin Franklin Medal (Franklin Institute)">Benjamin Franklin Medal</a><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
</div>
<ul><li>In 2018, Vinton Cerf was awarded Catalonia's International Award<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>

<li><i>Internet Activities Board</i>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc1120">1120</a>, September 1989</li>
<li><i>Thoughts on the National Research and Education Network</i>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc1167">1167</a>, July 1990</li>
<li><i>Networks</i>, <a href="/wiki/Scientific_American_Special_Issue_on_Communications,_Computers,_and_Networks" class="mw-redirect" title="Scientific American Special Issue on Communications, Computers, and Networks">Scientific American Special Issue on Communications, Computers, and Networks</a>, September 1991</li>

<li><i>A VIEW FROM THE 21ST CENTURY</i>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc1607">1607</a>, April 1, 1994</li>
<li><i>An Agreement between the Internet Society and Sun Microsystems, Inc. in the Matter of ONC RPC and XDR Protocols</i>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc1790">1790</a>, April 1995</li>
<li><i>I REMEMBER IANA</i>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc2468">2468</a>, October 17, 1998</li>
<li><i>Memo from the Consortium for Slow Commotion Research (CSCR</i>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc1217">1217</a>, April 1, 1999</li>
<li><i>The Internet is for Everyone</i>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc3271">3271</a>, April 2002</li></ul>
</div>

<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716"/><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 35em;">
<ul><li>Vinton Cerf, Robert Kahn, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www-net.cs.umass.edu/653-04/documents/cerfkahn.pdf"><i>A Protocol for Packet Network Intercommunication</i></a> (<a href="/wiki/IEEE" class="mw-redirect" title="IEEE">IEEE</a> Transactions on Communications, May 1974)</li>
<li>Vinton Cerf, Yogen Dalal, Carl Sunshine, <i>Specification of Internet Transmission Control Program</i> (<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc675">675</a>, December 1974)</li>
<li>Vinton Cerf, <a href="/wiki/Jon_Postel" title="Jon Postel">Jon Postel</a>, <i>Mail transition plan</i> (<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc771">771</a>, September 1980)</li>
<li>Vinton Cerf, K.L. Mills <i>Explaining the role of GOSIP</i>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc1169">1169</a>, August 1990</li>
<li>Clark, Chapin, Cerf, Braden, Hobby, <i>Towards the Future Internet Architecture</i>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc1287">1287</a>, December 1991</li>
<li>Vinton Cerf et al., <i>A Strategic Plan for Deploying an Internet X.500 Directory Service</i>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc1430">1430</a>, February 1993</li>
<li>Vinton Cerf &amp; <a href="/wiki/Bob_Kahn" title="Bob Kahn">Bob Kahn</a>, <i>Al Gore and the Internet,</i>  2000-09-28<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Vinton Cerf et al., <i>Internet Radio Communication System</i> July 9, 2002, U.S. Patent <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.google.com/patents?id=v7ALAAAAEBAJ">6,418,138</a></li>

</div>
<p>Cerf writes under the column name "CERF'S UP", and Cerf's car has a <a href="/wiki/Vanity_plate" title="Vanity plate">vanity plate</a> (registration) "CERFSUP".<sup id="cite_ref-2018-08_ACM_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018-08_ACM-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
